Local News

Two Important Telegrams from All Circles in This City 134

▲Supporting the Central Government's Warning to Gu and Chen

▲Issued at the Commemorative Meeting the Day Before Yesterday

The Shanghai Special City Party Department held a meeting of all circles in Shanghai to commemorate the 9th anniversary of the death of the Prime Minister in Guangzhou at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday. The details have been briefly described in yesterday's newspaper. The two important telegrams passed by the meeting are explored and recorded as follows:

▲Telegram of Condolences to Chairman Chiang: To Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Chiang Kai-shek in Nanjing: Having read the telegrams of May 28th, we respectfully understand your deep concern for saving the nation. Upon hearing this, we are filled with admiration. We believe that the Red bandits have been rampant for three years, and the provinces of Hunan and Jiangxi have suffered devastation. You could not bear the Red bandits' atrocities and the people's suffering, so you resolutely led troops into Jiangxi to suppress the bandits, braving dangers and rescuing the people from fire and water. All who have blood and spirit admire you. Our association sincerely represents the three million citizens of Shanghai, wholeheartedly supports you, and expresses our condolences. We hope you will appreciate our humble sentiments. Printed by the Shanghai All Circles Commemorative Meeting for the 9th Anniversary of the Death of the Prime Minister in Guangzhou.

▲Telegram Warning Gu and Chen: To Comrades Gu Yingfen and Chen Jitang in Guangzhou: Since the founding of the Republic of China, there have been constant wars and disturbances. Fortunately, all the generals and soldiers have worked together with one heart and fought in unison, which has enabled us to quell rebellions and achieve unification. We were looking forward to reorganizing the army and pacifying the Red rebels, to comfort the spirit of the Prime Minister in heaven and to satisfy the people's expectations. Unexpectedly, like a bolt from the blue, we heard that you comrades suddenly issued a telegram opposing Chiang. Now that unification and peace have barely begun, and the Red rebels are still rampant and need to be eliminated, your sudden actions are a destructive act against peace, and you comrades should bear the responsibility. The advance and retreat of party members should be in accordance with the party's orders. There is no such thing as individual free will, nor is it permissible for a few people to act out of personal likes and dislikes. Dedication to the party and the country is purely a sacrifice. There are no rights to speak of, nor is there any possibility of contention. Since Chiang's participation in the Northern Expedition, he has shouldered important responsibilities for the party and the country, and he has gone through countless dangers and near-death experiences. The world will have its judgment on his merits and demerits, so our association does not need to dwell on it. Even if you comrades have criticisms, you should formally submit impeachment procedures to the central government for a public decision. Instead, you are using troops to coerce, making alarming statements, imitating the old tricks of warlords, and following the path of rebellion. It is not surprising that Yan and Feng have done this, as they are opportunists who joined midway. You comrades are either advanced members of the party or revolutionary veterans, yet you are acting absurdly and resorting to such unwise tactics. This is what our association is greatly puzzled and saddened by. The central government is still showing leniency towards you comrades, repeatedly teaching you, fearing that you will start a war early and re-enact the tragedy of trampling on the people of southern China. Alas, Tibetan bandits are spying on Xikang, and Red bandits are rampant in Hunan and Jiangxi. Internal and external troubles are pressing in on us. If you comrades are determined to be the leaders of the rebellion, forgetting to attack, you are truly trying to place our nation and people in an irrecoverable situation. For you comrades, your infamous names will be forever recorded in history. For our suffering people, they will suffer another great calamity. Even if you comrades do not value your personal political lives, can you not think of the lives of the people in the homeland who are suffering? All the representatives of our association are both grieved and angry, and in great pain. Therefore, we issue a stern warning, hoping that you will pull back from the brink, salvage your late years, and fulfill your duty of sharing weal and woe. The future of the party and the country truly depends on it.

We hope that you comrades will carefully consider it in this time of survival and extinction. The Shanghai All Circles Commemorative Meeting for the 9th Anniversary of the Death of the Prime Minister in Guangzhou bows.

Two Foreigners Impersonate National Government Advisors to Purchase Large Quantities of Military Supplies 135

▲Briton Laif almost deceived

▲Zhang Fakui's younger brother is also involved

▲Everything exposed due to seal engraving

▲Details of the inside story still unknown

In the summer of the year before last, a bizarre case occurred in this city in which someone impersonated the American Vice Consul and defrauded the Chinese Yan Jiuling of a huge sum of money for the General Association's license movement fee. At that time, Chinese and foreign newspapers competed to report on it. One of the criminals in the case was the world-renowned military detective Youqin Beek, and the other was Gordon, who impersonated the American Consul. In addition, there was another suspect named Lewis. After investigation by the former Provisional Court, Beek was sentenced to nine months of imprisonment, Gordon was sentenced to three months of imprisonment, and Lewis was declared innocent. It has been two years since then. Beek and the other two have long served their sentences and regained their freedom. Now, except for Gordon, the other two were arrested by the police yesterday morning on charges of disturbing the peace and forging seals, and prosecuted in the Special District Local Court. Beek is Norwegian, and Lewis is Russian. The details of this accusation are very serious. According to a report made by a Briton, Mr. Laif, the owner of Laif Foreign Firm, to the General Police Station, it also involves the current incident in Guangdong. Mr. Laif's report mainly states that in mid-May of this year, Beek and Lewis were introduced to his firm by a Westerner from Jie Wu Sheng Company to order military supplies. The Westerner said at the time that Beek and others all had legitimate occupations and that no accidents would occur. He then agreed to meet them. Beek and others claimed that they had served as German military officers and are now employed by the Chinese government. Beek was appointed as a Colonel Military Advisor by the National Government, and Lewis was appointed as a Major General Military Advisor. Now, they were specially dispatched by the National Government to purchase military supplies. After negotiation, they agreed to sell them 6,500 rifles, 1,250 pistols, and other parts such as bullets, for a total price of 1,773,325 yuan, with 25% paid in advance, and the balance paid upon delivery of the goods. The above price was delivered to the Chase Bank, and the military supplies were transported to Shantou, Guangdong, for unloading. On that day, a draft agreement was signed. To be cautious, he notified the buyer that when signing the contract, each party must invite a notary to prove it. After the case was settled, Beek and others left. The next day, they returned to the firm with three Chinese men. After Beek and others introduced them one by one, it was learned that one of the three Chinese men, Zhang Faying, was Zhang Fakui's younger brother. The other two were purchasing committee members. They continued to discuss the matter and set June 12 as the official signing date. After they left, he felt that this matter was very suspicious. Since Beek and others were dispatched by the National Government, why were the military supplies transported to Guangdong for unloading? Therefore, he specially requested the British Consul in Shanghai to investigate with Nanjing. The British Consul advised that the military supplies could be sold, but it must be handled with caution. He then sent the draft agreement to Hallis Lawyer for review. Hallis Lawyer revised Article 7 of the draft agreement, stating that if the military supplies were to be transported to another place for unloading, the seller must be notified first, and all legal procedures must be handled by the buyer. He also requested the Chase Bank to pay attention to the buyer's power of attorney and the symbols they wore when the buyer paid the money. On June 12, the official signing date, he invited the Briton Carlo as the notary, and the buyer's notary was Zhu Caixue. The contract was made in triplicate, with the buyer and seller each holding one copy, and the remaining copy stored with the notary. The buyer's representative who signed was Zhang Faying, but Mr. Zhang did not arrive on that day. He only signed the contract and handed it over to Beek and others to take with them so that Zhang could sign. Unexpectedly, Beek and others took the contract and never returned. Because he did not know their address, there was no way to visit them. Recently, He Zixiang, the owner of Meitai Printing Bureau at 467 and 468 Zha Pu Road, whom he knew well, came to his firm and told him that a foreigner had gone to his place and asked him to engrave a seal. The foreigner also took out a seal and asked him to engrave it in the same style, and asked him to finish it by the 16th. After the foreigner left, he examined the sample seal and found that it was a seal with the name of Laif. Therefore, he came to inquire. When he heard He Zixiang's words, he was very surprised and asked He about the foreigner's appearance. According to He's description, he determined that this person was Lewis. Since he had limited time to engrave the seal, he must have needed it urgently. He requested that detectives be dispatched to investigate as soon as possible. Therefore, the head of the police dispatched Detective Chief, Russian Bebe Ning, Detective Harvey, and Chinese Detective Ma Wenda to wait near Meitai Printing Bureau on the 16th. At 4:35 PM, they saw Lewis enter the printing bureau to collect the engraved seal. After trying it once, he found that it was correct. Then, he took out a piece of paper with Western characters from his pocket and stamped it at the bottom with the newly engraved seal. He also borrowed another seal from the printing bureau and stamped it at the top. He seemed satisfied and put the paper in his pocket, paid the printing fee, obtained the receipt from the printing bureau, and abandoned the newly engraved seal in the bureau. As soon as he reached the door, he was captured by the detectives. The Western paper and receipt with the seal were found and taken back to the police station for strict interrogation. He confessed Beek's address, stating that he currently lived at No. 4 Lichar Road, while he lived at No. 24 Taili Shanfang, Xiafei Road, French Concession. The head of the police, in addition to ordering the Russian to be detained, went to Lichar Road to arrest Beek. Yesterday morning, he summoned the two witnesses, Laif and Carlo, and escorted Beek and others to the Special District Local Court. Chief Judge Xu Jashi took the chair in the First Criminal Court for trial. Qian Hongye, the prosecutor from the Procuratorate, attended the court to perform his duties. First, the police lawyer Ru Baoyi stated the reasons for the prosecution and the course of the case, and requested the issuance of two search warrants so that he could go to the residences of the two defendants to search for various evidence. Then, the Western detective reported that he witnessed Lewis using the seal outside the Meitai Printing Bureau. Laif also fully described the beginning and end of the purchase of military supplies. However, Carlo claimed that he was acquainted with Laif and was invited by Laif to sign as a witness, and he did not know the details. Chief Judge Xu then questioned Lewis. According to his confession, Laif Foreign Firm specializes in military supplies. He was introduced by Jie Wu Sheng and was an employee of the firm, specializing in managing loading and unloading matters. If the goods were shipped from Dalian to various ports, they were all managed by him. Now, he learned that Laif, the owner of the firm, was purchasing a large quantity of military supplies for Guangdong. He stole two copies of the contract and reported them to Song Ziwen, the Minister of Finance of the National Government. After receiving the report, Song left Shanghai for the capital the next day and sent a supervisor to Shanghai. Lewis confessed that Laif had originally planned to transport the military supplies purchased on behalf of others to Guangdong this month and hand them over to Zhang Fakui. After Lewis learned of this, he stole the contract and handed it over to me to take to Nanjing to report. Therefore, the contract is still kept in Nanjing. Laif, seeing that his actions were exposed, forged a seal to try to frame him. Lewis continued to confess that he went to Meitai Printing Bureau to order business cards, and he was scheduled to pick them up yesterday. Therefore, he went to pick them up yesterday and did not ask to engrave a seal. The Western paper found was not a copy of the contract, but a bill for military supplies shipped by Laif from Norway and Japan to Guangdong in May, requesting a settlement. The interrogation continued until 1:00 PM. The police lawyer then requested a postponement of two weeks to investigate the evidence. The two defendants were detained in the West Prison on Xiamen Road. Chief Judge Xu approved the request and adjourned the court. Beek and others were then escorted to the West Prison by the police for detention.

Zhang Zhijiang Discusses Pacification Work 136

▲Divided into two steps: bandit suppression and village cleansing

▲The notorious bandit Zhi Xiaotao was escorted to Yangzhou yesterday

Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner Zhang Zhijiang came to Shanghai yesterday morning. A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency interviewed him at his private residence. According to him, the Jiangsu pacification work is divided into two steps. The first step is bandit suppression, and the second step is village cleansing. The details of his discussion are recorded below:

▲Bandit Suppression Completed: Mr. Zhang said that there are many bandits in the counties north of the Yangtze River, and they must be eliminated by military suppression. However, most of the bandits are local villagers. When they see the army arrive, they hide their weapons and pretend to be good citizens. When the army leaves, they become bandits again. Therefore, to thoroughly eliminate the bandit scourge, we must focus on the second step of work. The bandit suppression work has long been completed, and we are now continuing with village cleansing.

▲Village Cleansing Work: Village cleansing is the most important part of the pacification work. Originally, this village cleansing work was also nearing completion. However, for the sake of thorough handling, we must continue to work in practice to achieve lasting peace. Last time, I went to the counties to inspect and told the county magistrates and local officials not to rely solely on written reports to complete the work, but to do it in substance. We must also have a clear understanding of the good and bad people in the villages. Currently, about two-thirds of the counties in Jiangsu Province have completed the work, and about one-third have not yet completed it.

▲Notorious Bandit Escorted to Yangzhou: Mr. Zhang came to Shanghai in person last time to negotiate with the French Consul to transfer Zhi Xiaotao, the notorious bandit north of the Yangtze River. Mr. Zhang said that he had been transferred from the French Concession after his arrival in Shanghai yesterday and had been escorted to Yangzhou for trial that day. The bandit fled to Shanghai a month ago. He committed crimes in more than 70 places north of the Yangtze River, killing, arson, and doing everything. After fleeing to Shanghai, he was hiding in the International Settlement. Hearing that the Pacification Commissioner's Office had sent someone to Shanghai to arrest him, he fled to the French Concession. After being captured in the French Concession, the criminal still hired a lawyer to defend him and tried to escape justice. Finally, after the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Songhu Garrison Command negotiated with the French side again, he was transferred to Yangzhou for trial yesterday, he said.

Chinese Director's Inspection of National Products Market Yesterday 137

▲Zhang Zilian States Reasons for Not Opening

The China National Products United Market, after being ordered to close by the Municipal Council, has been closed for nine days. The market is unwilling to open voluntarily. Yesterday, Chinese directors of the Municipal Council, among others, went to inspect the site. The details of yesterday's events are recorded below:

▲Chinese Directors Inspect　Yesterday, at approximately 10:00 AM, Municipal Council Chinese Directors Yu Qiaqing and Yuan Ludeng, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai, and Municipal Council Chinese Affairs Office official He Dekui, together arrived at the market for inspection. They were accompanied by Zhang Zilian and Hong Yanbin of the market, who assisted in observing the various construction projects recently completed in response to the Municipal Council's notification, to demonstrate the inaccuracy of the Municipal Council's claim that the market had not complied with the notification. During the inspection, Zhang and Hong

Page 14

both stated to the Chinese directors that today's purpose was solely to provide factual proof of the completed projects in response to the Municipal Council's allegations, leaving judgment of right and wrong to public opinion. A total of nine construction projects were inspected, which are recorded as follows: (1) Between the back stage and the kitchen of the east third floor, the former New World used wooden boards. Now, as per the Municipal Council's notification, the market has built a new brick wall. (2) Between the office and the amusement area of the east second floor, the former New World had no separation. Now, as per the Municipal Council's notification, the market has built a new brick wall to separate them. (3) On the east and west sides of the base of the escalator leading from the third to the fourth floor, the former New World originally used steel-reinforced concrete walls. Now, as per the Fire Department's instructions, the market has demolished these walls and created two new exits. (4) From the rooftop to the left and right escalators on the lower floors, the former New World had no handrails or wooden banisters. Now, as per the Municipal Council's notification, the market has installed wooden handrails on both the east and west escalators. (5)

At the base of the west escalator on the ground floor, the former New World had one existing exit. Now, as per the Municipal Council's notification, the market has built a new brick wall to block the exit. (6) At the base of the east escalator on the ground floor, the former New World had one existing exit with a door. Now, as per the Municipal Council's notification, the market has built new brick walls to block both the exit and the door, and created a new exit on the north side. (7) At the back stage of the Grand Peking Opera, the former New World had doors that were seven feet high and five feet wide, with single-leaf openings, two on the east and west sides. Now, as per the Municipal Council's notification, the market has enlarged the original doors and converted them into double-leaf doors that are fourteen feet high and seven feet wide. (8) Outside the back stage of the Grand Peking Opera, the former New World originally had a lead-sheet awning that was the same height as the doors. Now, because the doors have been enlarged and raised, the market has raised the original lead-sheet awning to eighteen feet. (9) In the small park, the former New World had a corridor with bamboo pillars and thin boards for the roof, covered with oil felt, with a section that was broken and dilapidated. Now, the market has replaced it with a corridor with wooden pillars and a lead-sheet roof, connected to the surrounding areas.

▲Zhang Zilian Speaks　Yesterday, Mr. Zhang Zilian, the founder of the National Products Market, issued a statement expressing his view that the market should not be easily opened. He stated, in brief, that on June 16, the Municipal Council sent representatives to request that the market first open and resume operations, which is a factual demonstration that the Municipal Council itself recognizes its actions were unreasonable. It also allows the public to understand the serious responsibility of the Municipal Council's illegal actions on June 9. The Municipal Council's illegal actions on June 9 were not simply a matter of infringing upon Zhang Zilian personally or infringing upon the rights of the market; rather, they involve violating agreements, infringing upon legal rights, and infringing upon the rights and business security of Chinese taxpayers in the settlement. If the facts surrounding this case are analyzed, the background of this illegal action contains elements of international competition, aiming for the complete destruction of the market's planned projects and preventing the market's plans for developing industry and the national economy from being realized, in order to fulfill their ambitions of aggression. Therefore, in order to defend the nation's legal rights, the people's dignity, and the rights of all Chinese taxpayers, I cannot easily open the market until this case is properly and legally resolved, so that China's legal and civil rights will no longer be despised and trampled upon.

▲Yu Qiaqing Speaks　Municipal Council Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing told a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday that the Municipal Council had arbitrarily closed the National Products Market due to the amusement department's facility issues, causing innocent businesses to suffer. He had raised the issue with Municipal Council Director-General Fessenden, who agreed that the market's commercial area could reopen immediately, but the amusement area would only be allowed to resume operations after the facilities were fully improved. He then invited Zhang Zilian of the market to discuss the matter, but no satisfactory solution was reached. He said that a response would be provided after the Municipal Council's regular meeting at 4:00 PM today.

▲Wu Jingxiong Speaks　Municipal Council Municipal Advisor Wu Jingxiong told a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday that Municipal Council Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing is currently negotiating with the Municipal Council regarding the case of the National Products Market being ordered to close by the Municipal Council. He said that he will continue to uphold his previous principles, do his best to uphold justice, and try to assist the Chinese directors in finding a good solution.

▲Taxpayer Meeting　The Chinese Taxpayers' Association held its fourth executive committee meeting yesterday and discussed this case. As a result, regarding the legal rights portion, the association will wait for the Municipal Council to respond to the previous letter before further review. As for the actual situation inside the market, since Chinese Director Yu and others have personally inspected it, they should uphold justice and report the facts to the Municipal Council board in order to resolve the matter as soon as possible.

▲Ministry of Industry Approves　The Shanghai China National Products Preservation Association received approval from the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating: "Your telegram has been received. We have investigated this case based on previous telegrams from the China National Products United Market and the Shanghai National Products Factories United Association, requesting that we forward a note to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to lodge a protest and engage in serious negotiations. We forwarded a note to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 13th of this month for their consideration and handling. Please be informed." This is the approval.

▲Group Support　Yesterday, the market received a telegram from the Wuhu County Chamber of Commerce and a letter from the Shanghai Antique Dealers Association. Declarations were also received from the New-Style Laundry Association and the Letterpress Printing Workers' Union, all expressing outrage at the case and offering their support.

▲Municipal Council Meeting　The Public Concession Municipal Council held a board meeting at 4:30 PM yesterday to discuss and dispose of the aftermath of the National Products Market. The meeting lasted for three hours. Those in attendance included Director-General MacNaghten, directors Peel, Brown, Kearney, Sheppard, Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Hu Mengjia, Fukushima, Okamoto, Municipal Council Superintendent Fessenden, and Municipal Advisor Wu Jingxiong. First, representatives from the Municipal Council Fire Brigade and the police department attended and gave a detailed report on the poor internal layout of the National Products Market, stating that the market's Peking Opera and other amusement areas were overcrowded, the interior was filled with flammable objects, and the emergency exits were blocked. In the event of a fire, the danger would be extremely high. In order to protect the safety of citizens, they requested the Municipal Council to ban the market. Subsequently, the Director-General submitted the issue of the aftermath for discussion. The meeting adjourned at 7:30 PM. This reporter then visited Municipal Council Superintendent Fessenden to inquire about the results of the meeting. He replied that the Municipal Council had decided to form a special committee to discuss the aftermath with representatives from the National Products Market. The special committee would consist of Municipal Council Western Director Brown, Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing, Chief Superintendent E.W. Catling, Fire Chief Tysoe, and Public Works Director Needham. External parties have expressed many dissenting opinions on this issue, which are of no help to the matter.

County Bureau Announces Reclamation of Wasteland 138

▲Deadline of One Month

The Shanghai County Government and the County Finance Bureau jointly issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Notice regarding the matter of wasteland reclamation. We have received instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, which stated: 'We have investigated the case of wasteland reclamation. The department previously drafted measures, which were presented to and approved by the Provincial Government Committee. We then ordered all relevant county bureaus to conduct thorough investigations and complete the process within the prescribed time limit. However, although the aforementioned measures stipulate that all cases must be completed within six months, there is still concern that prompt results may not be achieved without active implementation. Therefore, we are strictly setting measures and ordering all relevant county bureaus to promptly require the original operators to report to the bureau within one month for all uncultivated wasteland in the county, regardless of whether it has been cultivated or not. If they fail to report within the deadline, the operators will be deemed to have voluntarily abandoned their property rights. Farmers who cultivate the land will be allowed to report for reclamation, with certification from the Li Ce Shu (local record book), pay the price according to regulations, and be issued a stamped deed to manage the property, in accordance with Sun Yat-sen's principle of 'land to the tiller.' Farmers who have independently cultivated the land and have no owners must also report for reclamation within one month. If they fail to report within the deadline, neighbors will be allowed to report them and freely pay the price for reclamation, as a warning to those who are hesitant. Orders must be carried out; do not delay and miss the opportunity.' We have received these instructions and are issuing them to the county bureau chief for compliance, joint issuance, and widespread notification." We have investigated this case based on previous instructions from the Department of Finance, which promulgated the "Regulations for Reclaiming Uncultivated Wasteland in Jiangsu Province and Supplementing Grain and Promotion." We are issuing this notice to inform all residents of the county that all uncultivated wasteland, regardless of whether it has been cultivated or not, must be reported for reclamation within one month. Failure to reclaim within the deadline will result in the abandonment of property rights, and farmers who cultivate the land, or neighboring residents, will be allowed to report and reclaim the land. The deadline is imminent, and orders must be carried out. This matter concerns the protection of property rights, so do not delay and miss the opportunity. Be sure to comply."

Yu Dalun Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 141

▲Captain is Japanese Jinjiie Ishi

▲Reports Truth About Ship Collision

Yu Dalun, manager of the Haichang Company, colliding and sinking the British submarine Poseidon, has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, Yu Dalun arrived in Shanghai from Yingkou. This reporter made a special visit to the company. According to reports, Yu Dalun left Shanghai on the 7th and collided with the British submarine Poseidon at 12:09 PM on the 9th. The cause of the collision was that the submarine mistakenly navigated the channel, instead of avoiding outward, it turned and crossed in front of Yu Dalun. Yu Dalun was proceeding, according to course, unaware of the sudden change in direction. He immediately attempted to reverse, but within a split second, the collision occurred. Yu Dalun struck the bow, and the British warship struck the waist. The ship's hull was immediately breached, and seawater flooded the interior, causing it to sink extremely quickly. Our ship stopped to assist in the rescue, saving more than twenty soldiers from the ship. The captain of our ship, Japanese Jinjiie Ishi, immediately discussed the matter with the captain of the British warship, stating that the responsibility for the collision lay with the British warship, not Yu Dalun. The British captain also admitted his mistake, so he signed a document certifying his responsibility. Yesterday, after the captain arrived at the Yu Dalun Company on Yong'an Street to report the incident, he, along with the Shanghai manager and the ship surveyor, went to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company wharf in Yangjiadu, Pudong, to inspect the area of the ship's bow that had been struck. There was only minor damage, which will be repaired today. Regarding the shipowner's report of the matter, the Yu Dalun Company plans to slightly revise the text before publishing it, so that the public can understand the truth.

Customs Plans to Blow Up Sunken Dachang Steamer 142

▲Work Began the Day Before Yesterday

The Shanghai Times reports that after the Dachang steamer collided with the Dahua steamer outside Wusongkou in April and sank, the Customs dispatched five patrol boats to search for several days. Finally, the sunken location was measured to be about three li (Chinese mile) outside Songkou, in a key area for passing ships, obstructing navigation. It was necessary to blow it up. The Customs then contracted with the Tokyo Salvage Company to blow up the ship, agreeing on a daily wage of 77,000 yen and setting a broad timeframe of one year due to the difficulty of construction at that location. However, according to the company's estimate, the work could be completed in four months. The company began work yesterday (16th), first sending swimmers into the water to remove the masts and deck, and then blasting away the hull, to the degree that it is level with the bottom of the river.

American Ship Stranded on the Upper Yangtze Encounters Bandits 143

▲Stranded on Upper Yangtze The number one ship of the Upper Yangtze shipping company R-1 left Hankou on the thirteenth loaded with cargo for Chongqing. When traveling near the scenic sacred island of Yichang the water level retreated and the ship mistakenly ran aground. This area is known to be rampant with bandits, seeing the American ship have an accident, they gathered to attempt to rob the ship. Bandits drove small boats, fighting to get aboard the ship, creating a very dangerous situation.

▲Crew Resistance The crew and captain below were exceedingly worried, seeing the bandits armed with weapons, the crew also took up defensive weaponry. The bandits opened fire first, and the crew fired back, bullets flying from all sides.

▲Warship Rescue China's Second Yangtze Fleet was dispatched and sped to the rescue. When they arrived, the American ship was in the most dire circumstance. China's naval warship launched an attack on the bandits. Seeing the incoming warship, the bandits scattered and fled.

▲Crew and Passengers Rescued R-1 was run aground and lost the ability to maneuver. After the naval ship scared away the bandits, realizing the American ship could not be pulled from the sandbank immediately, they brought the ship closer, released sampans, and brought all the passengers, crew, and other personnel aboard. They prepared to send them to Yichang, not long after the American ship arrived in Yichang and the Yangtze rescue ship arrived to take the passengers and crew to Yichang.

▲Rescue of Ship The stranded ship will be rescued by the Yangtze rescue ship in about twenty four hours. While being towed, to protect against bandit attacks, China's naval warship will stay to protect.

Though the workers and passengers were scared, luckily nobody was hurt.

National Products Preservation Association Actively Prepares for 20th Anniversary 147

The China National Products Preservation Association was founded in the autumn of the Xinhai Revolution. Consolidated Tax Administration Reduces Tax on Cotton Yarn Seconds 148

The Consolidated Tax Administration of the Ministry of Finance replied to a letter from the Shanghai Chinese Cotton Mill United Association yesterday, stating: "In direct reply, we have received your letter of June 9, stating that cotton yarn seconds should not be classified as 'other types of cotton yarn' as referred to in the Consolidated Tax Regulations, and requesting that they be exempted from the consolidated tax in the same way as cotton waste. We have investigated that cotton yarn seconds are made from cotton, the same as cotton yarn. Although their selling price is lower than that of cotton yarn, they still have considerable value when transported and sold from the factory. They should be subject to the consolidated tax. Because their selling price is lower, this administration has specifically stipulated that the tax be levied on an ad valorem basis, to show that they are different from ordinary cotton yarn, which is taxed according to quantity. This has been in effect for a long time and has become a precedent. It is not appropriate to abolish it. We hereby reply for your information." After receiving the letter, the Yarn Mill United Association has separately notified all manufacturers for their information.

Confidential Document

The Second Volume of the Feetham Report (Continued) 162

▲Abstract Translation of the Fourth and Fifth Sections▲Chapter Five: General Discussion of "The Unique Characteristics of the International Settlement, Its Advantages and Disadvantages," and Discussion of Some of the Criticisms Included in the Statement Quoted in Chapter One. The existing administration of the International Settlement represents a vigorous and self-governing system within Chinese territory. What would be the actual result if the existing system were terminated and the International Settlement were completely handed over to Chinese administration at this time? This is one of the main issues for the future. Therefore, before listing the points of criticism one by one, it is necessary to first consider a broad issue as a starting point, which is not only relevant but also extremely important. What is this broad issue? What are the main characteristics of the International Settlement's administration that make it distinctly different from any administrative system in fully Chinese-controlled areas? The report indicates that the International Settlement's administration, based on the Land Regulations, differs from any system established in fully Chinese-managed areas due to the principles upon which it is based and the nature of the actual results it achieves. The unique characteristics of the International Settlement are summarized under two headings: 1. Principles; 2. Actual Results. The "principles" upon which the International Settlement's administration is based are the "autonomy" and "rule of law" described in Part Two. The openness involved in autonomy is noted in the report and it is mentioned that the publication of inspected accounts along with reports for submission to the ratepayers' annual meeting is an obligation of the Municipal Council. Although the importance of these principles is generally recognized, the direct causal relationship between the adoption of these principles in handling government affairs and the actual results achieved in administration is sometimes not fully understood. The actual results achieved are divided into (1) primary and (2) secondary. 1. Primary Results. The primary results can be summarized as two: (A) Safety; (B) Improvements in general living conditions. The security situation in the International Settlement, and the elements upon which this security relies, have been discussed in detail in the previous section. Improvements in general living conditions are the result of the provision and management of public services. The most notable are the construction and maintenance of public works, the protection of public health, the provision of education and sports facilities, and the provision of affordable water, electricity, power, and transportation. Regarding the issues of safety and improved living conditions, the work of the International Settlement Municipal Council, which has achieved such a degree of success under the special and limited conditions created by the general situation, is largely due to the adherence to the principles upon which the International Settlement's organizational law is based, in order to conduct honest and effective

Page 16

administration. Following these principles requires the acceptance of two main considerations as the work standard for the Municipal Council directors and their staff: (A) Respect for the public interest; (B) Compliance with the law. If the latter is interpreted in the practical work of administration, it means that all matters are handled in accordance with general laws and regulations, without any discrimination. I believe that the ability of the International Settlement Municipal Council to achieve such a degree of success is due to the adherence to certain principles in conducting honest and effective administration, but this does not mean that these principles are always fully implemented or that their achievements are beyond criticism. The Municipal Council is still far from this. Detailed criticisms are provided below. However, regarding the implementation of principles, the issue of respecting the public interest has been mentioned in previous chapters. The understanding of the public interest tends to be too narrow, and the idea that the so-called public interest should be interpreted as the interest of the entire society has not been fully recognized. I must also mention the honest and effective administration of the Municipal Council, but this does not mean that the Municipal Council's administration is completely flawless. It only means that, in general, it has maintained a high standard. In the management of such a large administrative organization as the Municipal Council, incidents of fraud, error, and omission are inevitable. It is difficult to expect that all bribery and corruption can be completely eliminated in the management of municipal affairs, which involves the employment of a large number of subordinates in an environment such as Shanghai. Some of this bribery and corruption has been long-standing and is considered excusable even if it is not permitted by law. If you want to limit this kind of evil to not exceed a considerable small range, only strict defense and persevering efforts can be successful. I want to emphasize that the achievements of the International Settlement's administration, which are greater than the achievements of Chinese municipal systems, should not be regarded merely as clear evidence of a comparison of the achievements of Chinese and foreign personnel, as some people sometimes assume. Rather, it is a matter of principle, that is, accepting certain principles as the principles to be implemented, and consistently applying these principles to the handling of ordinary government affairs. To establish an honest and efficient administration, there are two elements as follows: (1) Regarding financial matters, publication and auditing are the best guarantees of integrity. The Land Regulations stipulate that the Municipal Council's annual accounts must be audited (that is, audited by independent auditors) and published, and submitted to the annual public meeting for approval. (2) Public agencies, if they want to serve well, must provide generous treatment to their personnel. There must be reasonable and generous conditions in terms of both salaries and continued employment in order to attract talented people to serve them, and it must be guaranteed that the salaries or wages of the personnel employed are paid on time and according to the fixed amount. The terms of employment of the Municipal Council's staff, in any case, as far as senior staff are concerned, have obviously always followed a reasonable and generous policy. Its recent reforms have also raised the salary standards of junior staff, and the salaries or wages of all staff, from the highest to the lowest, have always been paid on time and according to the fixed amount, without any arbitrary deductions. If the Municipal Council and its personnel have any disagreement regarding the salaries due, the relevant staff or employees can sue the Municipal Council in the Consular Court. In fact, such cases of suing the Municipal Council have occurred several times. In this regard, the Municipal Council's position is different from that of the Chinese government authorities. The two elements mentioned above are very important for maintaining the financial integrity and high standard of administrative efficiency of the Municipal Council. These elements are closely related to the two fundamental principles of autonomy and rule of law upon which the International Settlement's administration is based. This is what should be noted. 2. Secondary Results. The secondary results of the Municipal Council's administration are not only important but also an indispensable element. This result is the development and prosperity of the International Settlement, as represented by its great industrial and commercial interests, large resident population, magnificent architectural facilities, and extraordinarily high land prices within the Settlement. It should be noted that if it were not for the strict respect for private property rights under the administration of the International Settlement, such high land prices could never have been created even in the most prosperous circumstances. Moreover, although the Municipal Council pays high prices to acquire land for the widening of roads and other public utilities, the high land prices, which result from the policy of insisting on respect for private landowners' rights, have a significant impact on increasing the economic resources of the International Settlement's administration. If there is any change in the status of the International Settlement, or any doubt arises about the continuation of the existing policy, the decline in land prices will be inevitable, and the economic resources of any governing body of the International Settlement in the future will also be reduced accordingly. I have already said that the various characteristics mentioned above give the International Settlement's administration a characteristic that is different from any system established in fully Chinese-controlled areas. This statement applies particularly to the two principles upon which the system is based: (1) Autonomy, including the methods of publication necessary for a true autonomous system; (2) Rule of law, in terms of the exercise of political power affecting private rights. As for the results, there is also the question of the degree of difference when comparing the International Settlement with the more advanced Chinese-controlled areas. In recent years, certain cities in China have indeed begun to make material progress and adopt more orderly and efficient municipal management methods. Most Chinese people also know the importance of this reform and are working to make it a reality. However, no matter how hopeful the success of this effort may be, when comparing the current Shanghai International Settlement with the Chinese-controlled areas, the overall standard of honesty and efficiency achieved by the Settlement's administration still stands out among the cities. Moreover, the improvements achieved in Chinese cities are not carried out under a system of representative government, but are mostly promoted by individuals who generally hold public office and have an enterprising spirit. These individuals, on the one hand, rely to some extent on the assistance and support of local people, and on the other hand, exercise some dictatorial powers. Therefore, the foundation of this reform is less stable. If the administrative personnel are changed due to external influences, civilized and progressive policies, if not based on the support of an organized autonomous society, can be endangered at any time. Only an organized autonomous society can recognize the value of the results of such policies and decide to obtain and maintain such results for itself. Civil government is not a guarantee against error, but in a society with autonomous bodies, voters are inspired by public spirit and understand their own interests, then their civil government, together with its necessary methods of publication, is indeed the best possible safeguard against administrative abuses. Such a society, after all, can know where the error lies and has the power to correct it. How is the value of the principles upon which the International Settlement's administration is based, as expressed by analytical methods, recognized by China's political leaders? The inclusion of the policy of adopting local autonomy within the accepted political procedures, and the public recognition of some of the main principles upon which the autonomous system must be based, can be regarded as extremely important factors for the future. However, hope is not the same as success. In terms of time and facts, the two may be far apart. Even when reform is still in the realm of empty talk, the difference and distance between the two are often overlooked by enthusiastic reformers. Criticisms of the International Settlement's administration are considered under four headings as follows: (1) The foreignization of the nature of administration. The main argument of all criticisms under this heading is that the senior staff of the Municipal Council are all foreigners, and that the Municipal Council's official documents are published in English. The report comments on these arguments as follows: It is very important to have educated Chinese participate in the responsible municipal administrative work and to interact with educated people in Chinese society, but partly because the Municipal Council's board of directors initially had no Chinese representatives, the board and the foreign community were slow to recognize this importance. As a result, the work of the Municipal Council was actually harmed, and a hostile atmosphere, mostly based on misunderstandings, developed among some Chinese people. Another part of the reason is that Chinese people feel that the Municipal Council's views on Chinese people are not given sufficient consideration, and that the International Settlement's administration tends to clearly ignore the interests of Chinese people and lacks understanding in interacting with Chinese people. It then mentions the recommendations of the Salary Committee and the methods of implementing these recommendations, and states as follows: A resolute and well-considered plan is currently underway to enable Chinese people to serve as senior staff members of the Municipal Council and to achieve both credibility and outstanding results. In the previous parts of this chapter, I have solemnly stated an argument, that is, the success of the Municipal Council's administration is due to the adoption of certain principles. The employment of Chinese people to hold senior positions does not necessarily conflict with the maintenance of the existing standards of the International Settlement's administration, as some foreigners commented. However, if good results are to be obtained, the pace of change must not be too rapid. Because this matter, like other matters affecting the administration of the International Settlement, should be gradually changed at a slow pace. Relatively speaking, the principles upon which the Municipal Council system is based are familiar to foreigners and less familiar to Chinese people. If the Chinese people who hold senior positions in the Municipal Council can use these principles successfully in the future, then these relevant Chinese people must first have sufficient time to gradually assimilate with these principles in the process of their personal practical experience. Moreover, there is another thing that must be remembered, that is, the difficulties encountered by Chinese people in senior positions are often more avoidable for foreign staff. Therefore, when there are special vacancies to be filled, the issue of whether to employ Chinese or foreign personnel is not only a comparison of talents. The world has people who are good at swimming, but are unable to use their skills when they encounter stormy waves. Old habits of administration, as well as the deeply ingrained customs and ideas of the people, all represent powerful currents. It is very difficult for Chinese individuals to proceed against these, and it may also be largely impossible for Chinese Council members. Regarding salary issues, or ordinary administrative matters, such as the application of general regulations without discrimination, this is also contrary to the old-fashioned ideas of the Chinese. I have already stated that I do not want to say that these difficulties cannot be overcome, but the fact that difficulties exist must be recognized. (2) The so-called common practice of corruption. There is a noteworthy fact, that is, although the issues raised by the Chinese Taxpayers' Association included a request for complaints, asking complainants to describe in detail the situation of Municipal Council staff accepting bribes or other improper conduct, this request only elicited a very weak response. Only the answer from the United Federation of Chambers of Commerce contained a comprehensive but uncertain accusation. I have already mentioned that there is a generally accepted fact, that is, as far as the board of directors and the senior staff of the Municipal Council are concerned, the achievements of the International Settlement are very clean, and maintaining a high level of financial integrity

is one of the characteristics of its administration. In addition to adopting preventive measures, the Municipal Council has always conducted thorough investigations of reported bribery cases,

and strictly punished offenders once the crime is established. (3) Policing. Due to the prevalence of armed crime in the International Settlement, especially kidnapping cases, criticisms of the International Settlement's policing have arisen. This criticism is mentioned in the report, and the special nature and difficulties of the crime problem in the International Settlement are discussed. In addition, excerpts from the report of the Chief of Police are also included and commented on as follows. It is noteworthy that the excerpts focus on two points: (1) The police force's efforts to prevent kidnappings and rescue hostages are greatly hampered by the lack of cooperation from the public, especially the families and friends of the kidnapped. (2) "The planning of kidnappings mostly does not take place within the International Settlement," and the main motive of this crime is also beyond the "authority" of the International Settlement's police force. Those who criticize the policing of the International Settlement often easily overlook these points when they discuss the issue of crime in the International Settlement, as if suppressing crime completely depends on the police efficiency of the International Settlement. It is then mentioned that gambling and private trafficking in opium soil are factors affecting the crime situation. The recent ban on dog racing in the International Settlement and the current situation of private trafficking in opium soil are also mentioned. Other criticisms regarding policing are also mentioned, including the inability of the police force to adopt any measures to suppress prostitution. The recommendations of the special committee organized in 1919 to investigate the crime situation in the International Settlement, and the implementation of the report of the committee in accordance with the "resolution passed by the ratepayers' annual meeting on April 7, 1920," are also described. The system of licensing prostitutes was adopted for a period of five years,

with the number of licenses decreasing year by year until the end of 1925, when the issuance of licenses was stopped. However, this plan has not proven to be effective in either abolishing prostitution or limiting prostitution. Therefore, how to devise a method to effectively control the evil that cannot be completely eliminated is still an unresolved issue. Moreover, according to the current law, the decision to stop the licensing system is an extremely difficult task for the police force. The current efforts of the police force are only to adopt a method

to limit the prostitution industry to certain areas and to prohibit soliciting along the way. However, recently, due to the general crime situation,

a large number of patrol officers are needed, and it is difficult for the Chief of Police to dispatch sufficient personnel

to carry out this work. According to the current situation, the entire issue seems to need to be re-examined. Those who criticize the International Settlement's administration are prone to assume that the prevalence of prostitutes in the International Settlement is due to the Settlement authorities' indifference to the welfare of the Chinese people. However, those who are harmed by the current situation are not limited to the Chinese people. In fact, under the current law, there is no licensing system, and the International Settlement authorities have no effective way to resist this evil. If a law is established that all those who open brothels or live by prostitution are guilty of crimes and should be severely punished, then the police force would have an opportunity to adopt measures that are much stricter than what they can do now. (4) The lack of sufficient facilities in Chinese schools and hospitals. The comments on the hospital issue described in Chapter Four, and the report submitted to the board of directors by the Education Committee in December 1930, are all mentioned. It is generally recognized that the criticism that there is no adequate provision for Chinese education in the International Settlement is well-founded, and that a more generous and progressive policy should be adopted for Chinese education in the future.
